Well Evaluation
Picture 1 Simmental 2-11 4TFH photo (Jenn Torres, Sunburst wellsite geologist)
1.0) Well Introduction and Location
1.1.1) Well Overview
Zavanna, LLC Simmental 2-11 4TFH [SW SE Section 35, T153N, R99W] is located
approximately 14 miles southeast of Williston in Williams County, ND. The Simmental 2-11
4TFH is a horizontal Three Forks well within the Williston Basin consisting of one lateral drilled
toward the south. Wellsite geologists will begin logging during vertical hole drilling, just above
the Base Last Salt marker in order to gather data to ensure a curve landing within the desired
target. The curve will be kicked off in the Lodgepole and landed in the Three Forks. Seven-inch
intermediate casing will then be set to isolate the target reservoir, after which directional drilling
and geo-steering techniques will be used to maintain maximum exposure to the target zone.
1.2.1) Vertical Offset Wells & Curve Landing Target
· Zavanna, LLC Simmental 2-11 1H [SW SE Section 35, T154N, 99W] located 90' west of the
subject well
· Zavanna, LLC Simmental 2-11 2TFH [SW SE Section 35, T154N, 99W] located approximately
60' west of the subject well
· Zavanna, LLC Simmental 2-11 3H [SW SE Section 35, T154N, 99W] located 30' west of the
subject well
Figure 1. Map of subject well and correlating offset wells (Source: NDIC website)
The TVD of our landing target, which represents the center of the target zone, was calculated by
assuming comparable formation thicknesses (isopach) between the subject well and offset wells
from the Base Last Salt Marker to the top of the target (Figure 4). As drilling progressed through
the various formation tops and markers, this target was continually monitored and updated as
necessary. A landing target of 11,228' TVD was calculated based off of the Gust 2-11 1H well
and its corresponding Base of Last Salt Marker. The landing target was adjusted to 11,227' TVD
after the final Lodgepole marker was logged. The curve was landed just below this at a depth of
11,231' TVD and 11,625' MD.
Figure 2. Curve TVD gamma signatures for the Simmental 2-11 4TFH (Jenn Torres, Sunburst wellsite geologist)
2.0) Wellsite Geology observations and Geo-steering
2.1.1) Lithology
Lithologic descriptions and sample analysis began in the Charles Formation in order to log the
Base Last Salt for curve landing purposes.
The Three Forks Formation is overlain by the Bakken Formation, which is recognized as the start
of the primary oil-producing zones. The Three Forks Formation is a complex petroleum system
within the Williston Basin that is sourced by the Lower Bakken Member. The formation
represents a series of transgressive-regressive events that were deposited during the Devonian
time period, and subsequently has undergone diagenesis creating its current lithologic make-up.
There are varying facies within the Three Forks which are commonly referred to as "benches".
The first bench of the Three Forks is the zone of interest for this well. It is comprised of lime
mudstone-packstone off white to cream-colored dolomite with varying degrees (trace to
common) of pale yellow to medium brown oil staining, interbedded with blocky, earthy-textured
shale with color varying from off white to mint green, and light to medium blue gray. Trace pale
to medium yellow oil staining was also observed intermittently on shale samples. Throughout the
lateral trace to common disseminated and nodular pyrite were observed.
2.2.1) Gas Monitoring
The overall gas trend of this well suggests the gas was the highest in the areas proximal to or
within the ideal target zone. Background gas averaged 1,800 units, with gas shows ranging from
approximately 1,500-4,500 units while drilling within this area compared to an average
background gas of 750 units, with gas shows ranging from approximately 700-1,400 units in the
areas above and below the ideal target zone. The largest gas reading was near end of the lateral,
just above target zone, and measured 4,491 units at a measured depth of 21,813'.

2.2.2) Gas and Oil Shows During Vertical and Curve Drilling
This well had significantly lower gas readings in comparison to the other three vertical/curves
drilled on the Simmental location. The background gas average in the vertical was 27 units for
the Simmental 2-11 4TFH, where the other three wells had average background gases above 40
units while drilling the vertical. The significant gas shows for this well came while building the
curve. There were fracture gas shows observed from the False Bakken through the Upper
Bakken interval that ranged from 126-412 units. The Middle Bakken had gas shows ranging
from 113-208 units. There were also fracture gas shows observed within the Lower Bakken
interval ranging from 172-460 units.
2.3.1) Geo-steering by Gamma Signature
The first bench of the Three Forks of the Simmental 2-11 4TFH is estimated to be 25' in
thickness, with alternating high gamma peaks and low gamma signatures. The target zone was
defined by Sunburst well-site geologists and the Zavanna prospect geologist as 6' thick, and is
noted in the below figure. The target interval was based primarily on a slightly higher porosity
zone and the ease of geo-steering.
Figure 4. Offset gamma signatures from the Angus 34-27 4TFH used for the Simmental 2-11 4TFH (Jenn Torres,
Sunburst wellsite geologist)
The drilling of this well purposed an interesting challenge. It was observed that drilling the zone
just above the ideal target resulted in extreme builds rates upon rotation, averaging 1.5 degrees of
build for every 90' rotated. After coming close to the Lower Bakken Shale, it was decided to
drill down to the lower half of the ideal target zone, and perform low side slides when an
inclination of 90° or higher was reached to avoid the area of high rotation builds just above the
ideal target zone. This was a successful approach as the wellbore remained in the ideal target
zone as drilling progressed, until slides became ineffective as the motor began to fail.
As drilling progressed it became apparent that the first bench of the Three Forks had thinned ~2',
beginning at approximately 17,465'MD. This interpretation is supported by the movement of the
wellbore in relation to its change in TVD as it passed through the gamma signatures defining the
ideal target zone. This thinning remained constant for the remainder of the lateral and is noted in
the below figure.

Gamma
Figure 5. Cross-sectional interpretation of the Simmental 2-11 4TFH borehole based on lithology, MWD gamma
ray, and ROP (Jenn Torres, Sunburst wellsite geologist)
Offset wells indicated that the Three Forks structure should drop 20' from landing to TD.
However, gamma signatures and sample analysis suggest that the formation had an initial
structural gain of approximately 29' (TVD) over the first 5,298' (MD) of the lateral. This yielded
an apparent up dip 0.31° for this interval of the well. Over the next 5,310' (MD) of the lateral,
gamma signatures and sample analysis suggest that the formation had a structural drop of
approximately 32' (TVD), yielding an apparent down dip of 0.30° for the second half of the well.
Over the entire 10,610'-long lateral, there was an estimated drop in TVD of 3', yielding an
apparent down dip of 0.02°. Geo-steering techniques exposed 94% of the borehole to the first
bench of the Three Forks. The well reached a TD of 21,835' on October 23, 2014.
2.3.2) Geo-steering by Sample Observation
In addition to the general lithology described earlier in this report, it has been observed that the
first bench of the Three Forks has differing lithologic characteristics depending on stratigraphic
location within the formation. The most helpful characteristics are apparent color changes of the
shale, and can be an invaluable tool for geo-steering. Samples taken while in the ideal target zone
(Picture 2) consist of mint green shale, which will fade to off white or blue gray with vertical
distance from target zone. Above the ideal target zone (Picture 3) is an example of the mint green
shale becoming off white to a very light mint green, and the presence of the blue gray shale
increases.
Picture 2. Simmental 2-11 4TFH ideal target zone sample consisting of light mint green shale with common
disseminated pyrite, and off white to cream dolomite with common oil staining.
Picture 3. Nelson 3-10 3TFH sample from above ideal target zone consisting of off white to light mint green shale.
Also present is the blue gray shale as well as nodular pyrite. The off white to cream dolomite has intercrystalline to
sucrosic texture with occasional oil staining.
Just above the second bench of the Three Forks (Picture 4) there is a cool gamma marker, with
loose subangular to rounded quartz grains observed. HCL and staining tests were used to verify
the grains to be quartz. This feature was localized to this cool gamma marker just above the
second bench and aided in adjusting steering accordingly to re-enter the ideal target zone. The
shale within this interval was a platy off white to very light gray. It was lacking color in
comparison to the mint green seen within the ideal target zone, and also helped to confirm the
stratigraphic location within the Three Forks.
Picture 4. Simmental 2-11 4TFH sample from just above the second bench of the Three Forks consisting of cream to
tan dolomite with trace light to medium brown oil staining. Also note the common loose transparent subrounded to
rounded quartz grains, which are exclusive to this zone of the first bench of the Three Forks.
3.0) Summary
The Zavanna, LLC Simmental 2-11 4TFH was spud on July 20, 2014, and reached TD in 28 total
drilling days on October 23, 2014. Samples from the Three Forks target indicated a mudstone to
packstone dolomite of variable oil staining with interbedded shale of varying color depending on
stratigraphic location within the first bench. The oil staining was described as trace to common
pale yellow to medium brown, and in some cases contained visible intercrystalline porosity. The
curve drilling revealed two significant intervals of fracture gas shows within the Upper Bakken
and Lower Bakken Shales. MWD gamma ray markers, sample analysis, and ROP were
successfully utilized to expose 94% of the lateral borehole to the first bench of the Three Forks.
The Simmental 2-11 4TFH awaits completion operations to maximize its production potential.
Respectfully submitted,
Jenn Torres
Jenn Torres
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
October 23, 2014

Zavanna Simmental 2-11 4TFH
Lithology
Rig crews and geologists caught lagged samples in 30' intervals from 9,470'- 21,835' (TD). All samples were
caught within compliance of North Dakota state regulations as well as the policies and procedures of Zavanna,
LLC. Cuttings were examined wet and dry using a stereo zoom binocular microscope. Dried samples were then
boxed and sent to the North Dakota Geological Survey. All depths are referenced to driller's depths.
9,470-9,500 DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE: mudstone, light-medium gray, microcrystalline, firm, earthy texture, no
visible porosity; ANHYDRITE: off white-milky white, cream, soft, massive, amorphous
9,500-9,530 DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE: mudstone, light-medium gray, microcrystalline, firm, earthy texture, no
visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: off white-milky white, cream, soft, massive, amorphous
9,530-9,560 DOLOMITIC LIMESTONE: mudstone, light-medium gray, microcrystalline, firm, earthy texture, no
visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: off white-milky white, cream, soft, massive, amorphous
Base Last Salt
9,576' MD / 9,567' TVD (MSL -7,287')
9,560-9,590 DOLOMITE: mudstone, light-medium gray, brown in part, microcrystalline, soft-firm, dense, earthy
texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare ANHYDRITE: cream-milky, soft, massive, amorphous texture
9,590-9,620 DOLOMITE: mudstone, light-medium gray, brown in part, microcrystalline, soft-firm, dense, earthy
texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare ANHYDRITE: cream-milky, soft, massive, amorphous texture
Ratcliffe
9,633' MD / 9,624' TVD (MSL -7,344')
9,620-9,650 DOLOMITE: mudstone, light-medium gray, brown in part, microcrystalline, soft-firm, dense, earthy
texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; rare ANHYDRITE: cream-milky, soft, massive, amorphous texture
9,650-9,680 DOLOMITE: mudstone, light-medium gray, brown in part, microcrystalline, soft-firm, dense, earthy
texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; trace ANHYDRITE: cream-milky, soft, massive, amorphous texture
9,680-9,710 LIMESTONE: mudstone, medium gray-dark gray, brown, microcrystalline, soft-firm, dense, earthy
texture, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain; occasional ANHYDRITE: cream-milky, soft, massive, amorphous
texture
Midale

firm, earthy-mottled texture, trace sparry calcite, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain

approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the
1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 2 & 11 T153N R99W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. In cases where a spacing unit is accessed from an off-site drill pad, an affidavit must be
provided affirming that the surface owner of the multi-well pad agrees to accept burial on their property
of the cuttings generated from drilling the well(s) into an offsite spacing/drilling unit. ZAVANNA LLC
must contact NDIC Field Inspector Jessica Gilkey at 701-770-7340 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing
point is: 450' south. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the
well head is: 10603' south.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division,
Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number,
drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m.
and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours
or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey
contractor shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion.
Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director
may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is
hereby granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing
on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well
records wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall
permit the Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or
controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to
have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time
upon request. The information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and
shall be available only to the Commission and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

Denver, CO 80202
